        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826566370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14885354918037600460">Liane Moriarty has done for Australia, what Maeve Binchy did for Ireland. They both brought the ordinary people of their countries alive on an unprecedented scale. Liane Moriarty is an international bestselling author. Look at her impressive bio on GR. <br/><br/>With Maeve Binchy's passing, a nation mourned. It was the first time an author received that kind of funeral attendance in living memory. Liane Moriarty has the world in an even bigger state of devotion. And the mystery is that you cannot pinpoint</span>
  <span id="freeText14885354918037600460" style="display:none">Liane Moriarty has done for Australia, what Maeve Binchy did for Ireland. They both brought the ordinary people of their countries alive on an unprecedented scale. Liane Moriarty is an international bestselling author. Look at her impressive bio on GR. <br /><br />With Maeve Binchy's passing, a nation mourned. It was the first time an author received that kind of funeral attendance in living memory. Liane Moriarty has the world in an even bigger state of devotion. And the mystery is that you cannot pinpoint the magic in her writing. Her stories are just talking in a language women can understand perfectly. Which makes it chick-lit of course. But there's an angle to it. A serious reality-check. <br /><br />Louise Penny did the same for Canada with her murder mysteries set in her Three Pine town and its inhabitants. <br /><br />It's the tone and the settings. The total ambiance of their stories. Whatever it is, we're gobbling it up.<br /><br />In <i>What Alice Forgot</i> the art, or rather secret, of staying married is defined. The two main protagonists are the sisters Alice and Elisabeth who bring their own smorgasbord of challenges to the table. <br /><br />Alice, being the main character, sustained a serious bump to the head during a spinning session, which temporary switched off her current persona, and started up her alter ego, confronting the person she has become since her 29th birthday ten years before. A decade of her life were wiped out. She had to rely on the people around her to redefine her, and the image was not a good one of herself. She was in the process of a divorce, her friend Gina passed away, she had a relationship with a new man, and did not know her three children from Adam. <br /><br />Elisabeth had trouble getting pregnant, which became a unsettling obsession for her, and her relationship with her sister was sort of non-existent. Their mother became a champion salsa dancer, marrying a man both sisters, and practically the whole community, had some social issues with. But Barb understood his soul and did not care what anyone thought about him or their relationship.<br /><br />That's all I'm going to reveal. Yep, we stop here! <br /><br />Many characters fill up the colorful background to the mystery of Gina's death, Elisabeth's bizarre actions and Alice's crave for perfection. The moral of the story is that you should use stilettos to catch a man, and use stilettos to get rid of him afterwards if you want to. In between the two choices, lies the secret of how to keep a man. Catching him is a different art from keeping him. All the men in the women's lives are strong characters with different appeals. Likable fellows with flaws. Well, yes, like all the female characters in the book, they have their reasons for being who they are.<br /><br />We're taken along for the ride and enjoy every moment, cheering them all on on this mysterious suspenseful journey to the biggest lemon meringue pie ever baked! Big enough for a whole community to absorb. We're part of it.<br /><br />LOVED THIS BOOK. ALL OF IT! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14885354918037600460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1956549876?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackey" href="/user/show/28470777-mackey">Mackey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28470777-mackey?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1956549876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12000034380058619307">What DID Alice forget? Well, after a fall at the gym, apparently everything! I'm beginning to truly adore these amnesiac stories - really! I am! How many ways can it happen? How long will it last? Will the husband be a baddie or a good guy? But I digress....this is about Alice. Why did she forget? She even forgot her own kids!! And none of the people from her past like her anymore including her sister or husband! Hmmmm....<br/><br/>While this all seems a bit trite when written this way, the book itself ac</span>
  <span id="freeText12000034380058619307" style="display:none">What DID Alice forget? Well, after a fall at the gym, apparently everything! I'm beginning to truly adore these amnesiac stories - really! I am! How many ways can it happen? How long will it last? Will the husband be a baddie or a good guy? But I digress....this is about Alice. Why did she forget? She even forgot her own kids!! And none of the people from her past like her anymore including her sister or husband! Hmmmm....<br /><br />While this all seems a bit trite when written this way, the book itself actually is quite marvelous. As Alice tries to rediscover herself and her memories, she learns a great deal about why she changed over the years, the events that led to those changes and how they affected all of those around her including, or most especially, her sister, Elizabeth. <br /><br />In a sense, this is a lot like "It's a Wonderful Life" as Alice learns to appreciate her old self once more. It was a very redemptive book; I think one of Moriarty's best. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12000034380058619307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1631076891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1631076891" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1631076891?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1631076891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17921178904930354159">What Alice Forgot by Lianne Moriarty is a 2010 PanMacMillian Australia publication. <br/><br/>With so many books out there, there is bound to be an author that slips by unnoticed, and for me, sadly, Lianne Moriarty falls into that category. <br/><br/>I knew her books were well received and popular, but I could never seem to find the time to fit one into my schedule. But, my local overdrive library heavily promotes her books, so finally, I took the plunge and put a couple of them on hold. <br/><br/>This book turned out to be </span>
  <span id="freeText17921178904930354159" style="display:none">What Alice Forgot by Lianne Moriarty is a 2010 PanMacMillian Australia publication. <br /><br />With so many books out there, there is bound to be an author that slips by unnoticed, and for me, sadly, Lianne Moriarty falls into that category. <br /><br />I knew her books were well received and popular, but I could never seem to find the time to fit one into my schedule. But, my local overdrive library heavily promotes her books, so finally, I took the plunge and put a couple of them on hold. <br /><br />This book turned out to be an excellent introduction to this author’s work and I can certainly see why her books are well liked. I absorbed this story like a sponge, savoring every nuance and subtlety. 	<br /><br />It was a coincidence, this book has an underlying Mother’s day theme, so it was fitting I found myself reading it this week. The story centers around Alice, a woman on the cusp of her fortieth birthday, who takes a serious tumble, and hits her head hard enough to cause severe memory loss… ten years of lost memories to be exact. <br /><br />Alice believes it is 1998, while in reality it’s 2008. A lot can happen in ten years, and for Alice it’s confusing, heartbreaking, scary, and sad. <br /><br />Also contributing to the story is Alice’s sister, Elisabeth and her adopted grandmother, each realizing, via Alice’s switch back to 1998, how they have lost their way or let time slip away from them. <br /><br />Amnesia plots are tricky in many aspects, but this story has a definite whimsical quality to it, despite the heavy issues at hand, and was handled adeptly. <br /><br />Alice and Nick are on the brink of divorce, but why? A tragedy has occurred, but what happened? Will Alice get her memory back? If she does, will she change or go back to being her old self again? <br /><br />Wouldn’t it be interesting to go back in time and basically get a do-over? What changes would you make? Were you a better person back then than you are now, or vice versa? <br /><br /> It’s so easy to allow our careers, and other outside forces, to take over, slowly infiltrating our lives, changing us and bending us until we lose sight of our real goals and priorities. If we were given the opportunity to see ourselves a decade into the future, would we like the people we became? Would be proud of our accomplishments, or would we feel sad by the way we traded love and relationships off for money, houses, and careers or allowed others to interfere or invade the goodness we had? Would we regret our choices? <br /><br />This story will challenge you to take a good hard look at your life and the choices you have made. Don’t forget the things that matter most, like your marriage, your children, and your family. Friendships are important and work is a huge part of our lives, but they shouldn’t be the most important thing, nor should they become an undue influence on our relationships or personality.<br /><br /> Many will see themselves in this story in one form or another, and can relate to busy, busy, busy lives, the irritants that pop up in married life, the ups and downs, the resentments that can settle in, the trite grudges, the awkwardness of coping with friends who split up and feeling loyalties divided, or maybe from having to compete with a friend for your spouse’s attention, with jealousy rearing its ugly head as a result. How common is Alice and Nick’s story? <br /><br />But, Alice is not the only one who has gone through incredible changes. Her sister’s struggles with fertility have left a mark on her, which has changed her personality and the dynamic of her own marriage. My heart went out to her, but I’m happy she considered all her options and was so proud of how she persevered in the end. <br /><br />The other story regarding Alice and Elizabeth’s adopted grandmother was also poignant and sweet, but I do wish we had been given more one on one conversation with her, instead of merely reading her thoughts via letters written to an old beau who died many years ago. <br /><br />Overall, this is a unique and thought provoking story, and perhaps a cautionary one too, but one that is full of second changes and hope that left me feeling at peace now that all is as if should be. I am really excited about this author now and have already queued up another of her novels. <br /><br />This one gets 4 stars<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17921178904930354159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2426459842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426459842" />
    <a title="Katie B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b"><img alt="Katie B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469412116p2/49444196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2426459842?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie B" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b">Katie B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425247440" href="/book/show/12377535-what-alice-forgot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=australia">australia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426459842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6341301280769913221">I'm normally not a big fan of amnesia story lines because they give me anxiety as it feels like torture having to wait for the person to eventually recall their memories. However, I gave this book a shot because I loved <i>The Husband's Secret </i> and <i>Big Little Lies</i> and thankfully, this turned out to be an enjoyable read. <br/><br/>It's 1998 and Alice is happily married and expecting her first child. Or at least that is what she thinks after hitting her head at the gym. In reality the year is 2008, Alice has t</span>
  <span id="freeText6341301280769913221" style="display:none">I'm normally not a big fan of amnesia story lines because they give me anxiety as it feels like torture having to wait for the person to eventually recall their memories. However, I gave this book a shot because I loved <i>The Husband's Secret </i> and <i>Big Little Lies</i> and thankfully, this turned out to be an enjoyable read. <br /><br />It's 1998 and Alice is happily married and expecting her first child. Or at least that is what she thinks after hitting her head at the gym. In reality the year is 2008, Alice has three children, and is in the process of divorcing her husband. What has happened in the last 10 years to get her to this place? Is it possible this memory loss will give her the opportunity to fix the wrongs in her life? <br /><br />Pretty much from the get go I was hooked as there were quite a few mysteries to play out such as why Alice and Nick were divorcing, why she had a strained relationship with her sister, and why Alice at 40 seems to have a different personality and interests than she did ten years ago. While I wouldn't say I loved this book as much as the other books I have read by the author, this one was a solid, entertaining read. There was one thing though I did not care for involving a story line that gets wrapped up at the end of the book. It's an annoying trope that I am sick of reading in books or seeing in movies and tv shows although I'm probably in the minority with that opinion. (Trying to be vague so I don't spoil anything). However, overall this is a good read even if you have a rough idea how it's going to turn out in the end. Definitely give this one a shot if you like Liane Moriarty's other books. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6341301280769913221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_624367495" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/624367495" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334166735p2/8665845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/624367495?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie">Debbie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=australian">australian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=head-disorders">head-disorders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=mostly-not-set-in-u-s">mostly-not-set-in-u-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=best-reads-2012-through-2019">best-reads-2012-through-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624367495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10926116565333924067">I love this book. Another terrific page-turner with well-drawn, interesting, and sympathetic characters. I get the idea that this is considered chick lit, but maybe it’s just that it doesn’t have enough U.S. exposure (the writer is Australian). Anyway, it’s not chick lit; it’s more of a well-written psychological thriller with all loose ends tied up nicely. The author seamlessly juggles and exposes the past and present lives of several characters, and does so with ease and talent; it’s nothing s</span>
  <span id="freeText10926116565333924067" style="display:none">I love this book. Another terrific page-turner with well-drawn, interesting, and sympathetic characters. I get the idea that this is considered chick lit, but maybe it’s just that it doesn’t have enough U.S. exposure (the writer is Australian). Anyway, it’s not chick lit; it’s more of a well-written psychological thriller with all loose ends tied up nicely. The author seamlessly juggles and exposes the past and present lives of several characters, and does so with ease and talent; it’s nothing short of brilliant. <br /><br />The plot: A woman bumps her head and forgets ten years of her life. Of course, it made me try to imagine what that would be like. Emotionally, you’re the optimistic and care-free self from the old days instead of the responsible, loving mother of the present. Imagine suddenly having to raise three children who are complete strangers to you! And imagine how much your relationship with your husband and sister would change over 10 years, and how weird it would be when you’re emotionally thrown back into the good days (where you’re happy, hopeful, poorer, and childless) when you are of course in the very different and complicated present day (where you’re sterner, more skeptical, richer, and childful)—and of which you know nothing. They are treating you so differently and you have to suddenly wonder, who IS this person that I apparently have become? And what has happened to the people I love?—they are older and sadder and madder. They relate to you as the person you really are in the present, but emotionally you are no longer that person but an earlier version of her—more innocent and hopeful—and you are confused and don’t know how to act. It’s a super interesting idea and the author works it with brilliance. I want to check out more from this writer. Highly recommend. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10926116565333924067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16050366446110599782"><b>Clever and funny.</b><br/><br/>As with all of Moriarty's books, this one's filled with very rich, fully-developed characters.   <span id="freeText16050366446110599782" style="display:none"><b>Clever and funny.</b><br /><br />As with all of Moriarty's books, this one's filled with very rich, fully-developed characters. She's an extremely gifted, very entertaining storyteller, as so many people already know. This one's a great read.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307601275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16400027915172597622">Set in Australia during 2008, <i>What Alice Forgot</i> tells the story of thirty-nine year old Alice Love. She is a single mother of three and is going through a messy divorce. One day at the gym, Alice has an accident, bumps her head and forgets the past ten years of her life. Alice wakes up thinking it's the year 1998 and she's 29 years old, she's madly in love with her husband Nick and they're about to have their first child! <br/><br/>I really loved this novel! The plot was very intriguing, compelling and we</span>
  <span id="freeText16400027915172597622" style="display:none">Set in Australia during 2008, <i>What Alice Forgot</i> tells the story of thirty-nine year old Alice Love. She is a single mother of three and is going through a messy divorce. One day at the gym, Alice has an accident, bumps her head and forgets the past ten years of her life. Alice wakes up thinking it's the year 1998 and she's 29 years old, she's madly in love with her husband Nick and they're about to have their first child! <br /><br />I really loved this novel! The plot was very intriguing, compelling and well-written with an interesting and unique premise. I loved the author's writing style. The story was very funny and some parts were quite touching and made me want to cry. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I lost my "Gina" too. My best friend died quite suddenly a year ago so that part of the novel when Alice remembers her friend's death really hit a nerve with me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The characters were all well-developed, vivid and believable. I found it easy to relate to Alice and the other characters. I was unable to put this book down for long. I was desperate to find out what was going to happen next! <br /><br />Alice discovers her life has changed dramatically but sees it from the point of view of her twenty-nine year old, carefree, fun loving self. Alice doesn't like the uptight, bitter person she has become. Alice re-examines her relationships with those people closest to her, in particularly her soon-to-be ex-husband Nick and her sister Elizabeth. The novel made me think about how my own life has changed in the last ten years and what would the "me" of ten years ago think of the person I am now? I liked that the author had included Alice's sister's journal entries and her grandmother's letters. This helped me see Alice from other people's perspectives, learn more about the character's background and see how much this experience had changed Alice. <br /><br />I was sorry when this novel came to an end. I just wanted it to go on and on. I really loved the twist at the end and I was happy that Alice had ending up with that person. This is one book I will definitely re-read over and over again. This novel is now one of my favourite books and will most likely make it onto my top 10 list of the best books I've read in 2013! I can't wait to read more of Liane Moriarty's books!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16400027915172597622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R1LeRC9IfT/kASMnw8KS9nSq0hbjIowKG67UEwlVgjR9dLeWlBa0V0Mql0Y0N5gpovU13i2vAm1A0JKixBZwrg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

And no one embodies this spirit more than Elena Richardson, whose guiding principle is playing by the rules.\n\nEnter Mia Warren--an enigmatic artist and single mother--who arrives in this idyllic bubble with her teenaged daughter Pearl, and rents a house from the Richardsons. Soon Mia and Pearl become more than tenants: all four Richardson children are drawn to the mother-daughter pair. But Mia carries with her a mysterious past and a disregard for the status quo that threatens to upend this carefully ordered community.\n\nWhen old family friends of the Richardsons attempt to adopt a Chinese-American baby, a custody battle erupts that dramatically divides the town--and puts Mia and Elena on opposing sides. Suspicious of Mia and her motives, Elena is determined to uncover the secrets in Mia\'s past. But her obsession will come at unexpected and devastating costs.\n\nLittle Fires Everywhere explores the weight of secrets, the nature of art and identity, and the ferocious pull of motherhood--and the danger of believing that following the rules can avert disaster.Named a Best Book of the Year by: People, The Washington Post, Bustle, Esquire, Southern Living, The Daily Beast, GQ, Entertainment Weekly, NPR, Amazon, Barnes &amp; Noble, iBooks, Audible, Goodreads, Library Reads, Book of the Month, Paste, Kirkus Reviews, St. Louis Post-Dispatch, and many more...\n\nPerfect for book clubs!       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty">About Liane Moriarty</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1459827224p3/322069.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3198783639612155195">Liane Moriarty is the Australian author of six internationally best-selling novels, Three Wishes, The Last Anniversary, What Alice Forgot, The Hypnotist's Love Story and the number 1 New York Times bestsellers, The Husband's Secret and Big Little Lies. <br/><br/>Her breakout novel The Husband's Secret sold over three million copies worldwide, was a number 1 UK bestseller, an Amazon Best Book of 2013 and has</span>
  <span id="freeText3198783639612155195" style="display:none">Liane Moriarty is the Australian author of six internationally best-selling novels, Three Wishes, The Last Anniversary, What Alice Forgot, The Hypnotist's Love Story and the number 1 New York Times bestsellers, The Husband's Secret and Big Little Lies. <br /><br />Her breakout novel The Husband's Secret sold over three million copies worldwide, was a number 1 UK bestseller, an Amazon Best Book of 2013 and has been translated into over 40 languages. It spent over a year on the New York Times bestseller list. CBS Films has acquired the film rights. <br /><br />With the launch of Big Little Lies, Liane became the first Australian author to have a novel debut at number one on the New York Times bestseller list. An HBO series based on Big Little Lies is currently in production, starring Nicole Kidman and Reese Witherspoon. <br /><br />Writing as L.M. Moriarty, Liane has also written a children's book series, The Petrifying Problem with Princess Petronella, The Shocking Trouble on the Planet of Shobble and The Wicked War on the Planet of Whimsy. <br /><br />Liane lives in Sydney with her husband, son and daughter. Her new novel, Truly Madly Guilty, will be released in July 2016. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3198783639612155195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
